Krishnamurti', u'\n', u'Vivekananda', u'\n', u'Yogananda', u'\n', u'Ramachandra Dattatrya Ranade', u'\n', u'Mata Amritanandamayi', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Other topics', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Calendar', u'\n', u'Criticism', u'\n', u'Denominations', u'\n', u'Iconography', u'\n', u'Mythology', u'\n', u'Nationalism', u'\xa0', u'(', u'Hindutva', u')', u'\n', u'Persecution', u'\n', u'Pilgrimage sites', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Hinduism and Jainism', u'\xa0/ ', u'and Judaism', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Hinduism by country', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Glossary of Hinduism terms', u'\n', u' ', u'Hinduism portal', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'v', u'\n', u't', u'\n', u'e', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Rama', u' (', u'/', u'\u02c8', u'r', u'\u0251\u02d0', u'm', u'\u0259', u'/', u';', u'[1]', u' ', u'Sanskrit', u': \u0930\u093e\u092e ', u'R\u0101ma', u') or ', u'Sr\u012b R\u0101machandra', u' (', u'Sanskrit', u'\xa0: \u0936\u094d\u0930\u0940 \u0930\u093e\u092e\u091a\u0928\u094d\u0926\u094d\u0930) is the ', u'seventh', u' ', u'avatar', u' of the Hindu God ', u'Vishnu', u'. He is the central figure of the ', u'Hindu epic', u' ', u'Ramayana', u', which is the principal narration of the events connected to his incarnation on Earth, his ideals and his greatness. Rama is one of the many deities in ', u'Hinduism', u' and especially of the various ', u'Vaishnava', u' sects. Religious texts and scriptures based on his life have been a formative component in numerous cultures of ', u'South', u' and ', u'Southeast Asia', u'.', u'[2]', u' Along with ', u'Krishna', u', Rama is considered to be one of the most important avatars of Vishnu. In Rama-centric sects, he is considered the Supreme Being, rather than an avatar.', u'\n', u'Born as the eldest son of ', u'Kaushalya', u' and ', u'Dasharatha', u', ruler of ', u'Kosala', u" Kingdom (now in Uttar Pradesh), Rama is referred as ''", u'Maryada Purushottama', u'"', u'[3]', u' within Hinduism, which literally means ', u'the Perfect Man', u' or ', u'Lord of Self-Control', u' or ', u'Lord of Virtue', u'. His wife ', u'Sita', u' is considered by Hindus to be an avatar of ', u'Lakshmi', u' and the embodiment of a great woman.', u'[3]', u'[4]', u'\n', u'Rama and his brothers ', u'Lakshman', u', ', u'Bharat', u', ', u'Shatrughna', u' were the "chaturvyuha" expansions of Vishnu (', u'Vasudev', u', ', u'Sankarshan', u', ', u'Pradyumna', u', ', u'Aniruddha', u"). Rama's life and journey is one of adherence to ", u'dharma', u" despite harsh tests and obstacles and many pains of life and time. For the sake of his father's honour, Rama abandons his claim to Ayodhya's throne to serve an exile of fourteen years in the forest.", u'[5]', u' His wife Sita and brother ', u'Lakshmana', u' decide to join him, and all three spend the fourteen years in exile together. While in exile, Sita is kidnapped by ', u'Ravana', u', the king of ', u'Lanka', u". After a long and arduous search, Rama fights a colossal war against Ravana's armies. In a war of powerful and magical beings, greatly destructive weaponry and battles, Rama slays ", u'Ravana', u' in battle and liberates his wife.', u'[6]', u' Having completed his exile, Rama returns to be crowned king in Ayodhya and eventually becomes emperor,', u'[5]', u' rules with happiness, peace, duty, prosperity and justice\u2014a period known as ', u'Rama Rajya', u'.', u'\n', u'The legend of Rama is deeply influential and popular in the societies of the ', u'Indian subcontinent', u' and across ', u'South East Asia', u'. Rama is revered for his unending compassion,', u'[7]', u' courage and devotion to religious values and duty. The deity ', u'Hanuman', u' declared Rama to be a supreme being, and said that, by chanting the name of Lord Rama, all earthly problems may be resolved. By chanting the name of lord Rama 10 million times, ', u'Moksha', u' can be achieved.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Contents', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'1', u' ', u'Etymology', u'\n', u'2', u' ', u'Literary sources', u'\n', u'3', u' ', u'Balkand', u'\n', u'4', u' ', u'Rama and Sita', u'\n', u'5', u' ', u"Sita's Exile", u'\n', u'\n', u'5.1', u' ', u'Children', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'6', u' ', u'Later life', u'\n', u'7', u' ', u'Abilities', u'\n', u'8', u' ', u'Maryada Purushottama', u'\n', u'9', u' ', u'Companions', u'\n', u'\n', u'9.1', u' ', u'Bharata and Lakshmana', u'\n', u'9.2', u' ', u'Jatayu, Hanuman & Vibhishana', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'10', u' ', u'Rama In War', u'\n', u'\n', u'10.1', u' ', u'Varuna', u'\n', u'10.2', u' ', u'Facing Ravana', u'\n', u'10.3', u' ', u'Rama Rajya', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'11', u' ', u'International Influence', u'\n', u'12', u' ', u'Rama Worship', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.1', u' ', u'Festivals', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.1.1', u' ', u'Rama Navami', u'\n', u'12.1.2', u' ', u'Vijayadashmi', u'\n', u'12.1.3', u' ', u'Diwali', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.2', u' ', u'Temples', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'13', u' ', u'In Jainism', u'\n', u'14', u' ', u'See also', u'\n', u'15', u' ', u'Notes', u'\n', u'16', u' ', u'References', u'\n', u'17', u' ', u'Further reading', u'\n', u'18', u' ', u'External links', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Etymology', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This article ', u'needs additional citations for ', u'verification', u'. Vashishta to the left', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u"At Mithila,Rama breaks Shiva's bow and Janaka arranges the marriage of his daughter Sita to Rama.", u'[27]', u' The ', u'Wedding of Rama and Sita', u' concerns two entities coming together to form a whole. An Indian marriage forges an alliance not only between two people, but also two families. The marriage of Sita and Rama creates an alliance between two people, two families, and two kingdoms: ', u'Mithila', u', home of Sita and ', u'Kosala', u", home of Rama. Furthermore, Rama's marriage to Sita on Earth parallels the celestial union of ", u'Vishnu', u' and ', u'Lakshmi', u'; each deity took birth on Earth, and so when Rama marries Sita, he is actually reuniting with his divine consort Lakshmi, Goddess of Good Fortune, who brings prosperity to Kosala. At an allegorical level, the union of Rama and Sita represents the relationship between God and the devotee, with Rama as the beloved divine king and Sita as his devotee. Finally, at a societal level, the dance drama brings together north and south Indian dance traditions.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u"Sita's Exile", u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. He does so after receiving word that some of his subjects in Ayodhya believed that Sita was unfit due to her long captivity in Ravana's city. As a king is expected to uphold moral principles, Rama reluctantly banished Sita in order to uphold his duty. Sita took refuge under the noble sage ", u'Valmiki', u'.', u'\n', u'A legend by Rishi ', u'Agastya', u' in the epic states that ', u'Vishnu', u' in a previous age had been cursed by ', u'Rishi Bhrigu', u", whose wife had been killed by Vishnu for sheltering his enemies escaping from battle. The Rishi condemns Vishnu to be denied for a long age the companionship of his soul mate, just as Vishnu, had deprived the Rishi of his loving wife. Thus Rama, Vishnu's incarnation, must live the rest of his life without Sita.", u'\n', u'Many Hindus, such as the followers of ', u'Sri Vaishnavism', u', consider this entire section of the Ramayana to be interpolated and thus they do not accept the authenticity of this story claiming that Sita was banished.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Sita', u'(far right), Rama(center), ', u'Lakshmana', u'(far left) and ', u'Hanuman', u'(below seated) at ', u'Bhaktivedanta Manor', u', a temple in Watford(England)', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'An alternate narration of ', u'Ramayana', u' does not state it so. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Main articles: ', u'Kusha (Ramayana)', u' and ', u'Lava (Ramayana)', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nLava and Kusha, the sons of Rama', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'According to legend, ', u'Kusha', u' and ', u'Lava', u' are twin sons of Lord Rama and Sita. Born in the forest after banishment of Sita from ', u'Ayodhya', u', the twins were educated and trained in military skills as their mother took refuge in Sage ', u'Valmiki', u"'s ", u'ashram', u', located in a forest on the banks of ', u'Tamsa river', u'.', u'\n', u'As Rama performed the ', u'Ashvamedha', u' ', u'Yajna', u", a horse strayed into their forest, Rama sent Hanuman to retrieve the horses. Rama's sons Lava and Kusha captured the horses. Hanuman, seeing Lava and Kusha recognised that they were the son's of Rama. He let them capture him and tie him up. There Hanuman started meditating on the name Rama. Worried Rama sent his brothers to look for the horses. As they saw Hanuman tied up and two boys guarding him, they thought that the two boy had stolen the horses. So Rama's brothers started attacking Lava and Kusha. Although Rama's brothers should have won, but Lava and Kusha defeated them all, knocking them unconscious. Lava and Kusha were protected by Hanuman. Then Rama himself went looking for the horses fearing that Hanuman and his brothers had been attacked. On his way there, Rama intuitively knew that Lava and Kusha were his sons and purposely slept on his chariot to delay tension and confrontation with his sons as he knew it would be inappropriate for a father to fight his sons. Upon reaching the battlefield, sage Valmiki interrupted the potential battle between father and sons by explaining to Rama that Lava and Kusha were his sons. A familial reunion took place.", u'\n', u"When Devi Sita found out that Lava and Kusha had defeated Ayodhya's forces, she proudly revealed their/her identity. Rama desired Sita and his sons to live with him in his kingdom, but as this took place, the general population of the kingdom resented Sita from returning. In response, Sita forsaked her life and sought final refuge in the arms of her mother Bhumidevi, the Goddess Mother Earth and ultimately returned to Rama in the form of Vishnu in Vishnu's abode - indicating that forced separation from her beloved husband is only limited in life on Earth compared to her eternal union with her beloved in life after death.", u'\n', u'Later life', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. During this period, people were healthy, holy, satisfied and lived with complete peace and harmony. There was no evil, no wars, no natural calamity and no diseases. Rama ruled the whole Earth without using military force as all kings submitted themselves to him.', u'\n', u'His brothers Bharata and Shatrughna settled in their later lives. Bharata, with the help of his uncle Yudhajita, conquered the eastern land of the Gandharvas and ruled it. Shatrughna slew the Asura Lavana and founded the city of Mathura. Rama acquired a rare gem from Rishi ', u'Agastya', u' that entombed the powers of the gods ', u'Indra', u', ', u'Varuna', u', ', u'Yama', u' and ', u'Kubera', u', which helped the king rule efficiently. Valmiki Ramayana mentions an abode named ', u'Santanaka', u' invested with all spiritual qualities and located beyond Brahmaloka, which was attained by all followers of Rama, after Rama along with his brothers, entered into Vaishnava potency. Lava and Kusha ruled ', u'Kosala', u' and continued the solar race.', u'\n', u'Abilities', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(June 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Rama was a great king and warrior. He had exceptional mastery over the Vedas, the scriptures, administration and warfare under the tutelage of Brahmarshi Vasishtha, son of Lord Brahma. He also acquired mastery over celestial weapons from Sage Vishwamitra. Agastya gave him a divine jewel, a divine bow, a quiver of arrows, an impenetrable armour and a sword. Rama and his brothers had conquered the World before going to exile.', u'\n', u"Rama also possessed tremendous strength, as he was easily able to lift and break the mighty bow of Shiva that required 5000 strong men to pull it. He also once sent the skeleton of the gigantic Asura Dundubhi flying over 130\xa0km by a flick of his toe. Sage Parashurama, renowned for his skills in warfare granted Rama the full power of his penances, contributing to Rama's prowess.", u'\n', u'After the death of Ravana, Lord Brahma agreed to grant any boon to Rama. Rama asked to be freed of his sins, to always remain virtuous and to become invincible in battle. Brahma granted all these boons.', u'\n', u'Maryada Purushottama', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nLord Rama tired of asking a non-responding ', u'Varuna', u' (God of the oceans) to help him, and took up the ', u'Brahmastra', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'As a person, Rama personifies the characteristics of an ideal person(purushottama),', u'[3]', u'[28]', u" who is to be emulated. He had within him all the desirable virtues that any individual would seek to aspire, and he fulfils all his moral obligations(maryada). Rama's purity and piety in his intentions and actions inspires affection and devotion for him from a variety of characters from different backgrounds. For example, he gave up his rightful claim to the throne, and agreed to go into exile for fourteen years, to fulfill the vow that his father had given to Kaikeyi, one of King Dasharatha's wives. This is in spite of the fact that Kaikeyi's son, Bharat, begged him to return to Ayodhya and said that he did not want to rule in place of Rama. But Rama considered his dharma as a son above that of his own birthright and his life's ambition. For such supreme sacrifices, and many other qualities, Rama is considered a ", u'maryada purushottama', u' or the best of upholders of Dharma, God in the form of an exemplary human.', u'[29]', u'\n', u'Some of his ideals are as follows:', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u"1. At the time when it was normal for kings to have more than one wife, Rama gave the ideal of having a single wife. In Balakanda of Valmiki Ramayana, it is written that Rama and Sita resided in each other's heart.", u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u"2. Rama always followed his promise at any cost. In fact, he went to forest to make his father's promise to Kaikeyi true. Another instance was when, he had promised the spirit of time that during their conversation, if anyone was to intrude, Rama would have pronounce an instant death sentence upon the individual. They were intruded upon by his beloved younger brother ", u'Lakshmana', u" and to keep his part of the promise, pronounced the death sentence. There are many examples of Rama's promises that he kept. Most important are the promise to sages to save their lives from ", u'Rakshasas', u', getting back ', u'Sugreeva', u"'s kingdom, making ", u'Vibhishana', u' the king of ', u'Lanka', u'.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u'3. Excellent friend: Rama had very touching relations with his friends irrespective of their status. Some of his friends are Nishada-raja Guha, King of ', u'Nishadha', u'(a caste whose profession was hunting the birds), Sugreeva(the ', u'Vanara', u' king) and ', u'Vibhishana', u'.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u"4. Even towards his enemies, Rama showed great nobility and virtue. To gather information about the enemy army's strengths and weaknesses, ", u'Ravana', u' sent two of his spies, Suka and Sarana, to the ', u'Vanara', u' camps. Disguised as ', u'Vanaras', u' they blended into the enemy camp, but ', u'Vibhishana', u" saw through their deceit. The duo sought Rama's protection when the monkey warriors thrashed them. Rama gave them refuge. He then asked them what their mission was and whether they fulfilled it. After listening to them, he sent for a ", u'Vanara', u' to give them a proper tour of all the ', u'Vanara', u' camps and give them all the information they desired about the major soldiers and their strengths. He then told the spies to give this message to ', u'Ravana', u'. "Tomorrow morning, I will destroy all of ', u'Lanka', u'. Keep all sides of your palace well defended and be ready with all of your men by sunrise." The spies were greatly astonished with Rama\'s charisma, courage and adherence to the codes of war. After Rama gave them leave, they knew that their king was bound to lose against this virtuous and courageous man.', u'\n', u'When ', u'Ravana', u' first fought with Rama, Rama defeated him to such an extent that ', u'Ravana', u' lost his charioteer, horses, chariot, flag, weapons and armor. Though the situation was at his advantage, Rama instead praised ', u'Ravana', u' for a great fight that day and asked him to retire and take rest, as he must be quite tired. Denouncing his mother, Bharata proclaims to the city that he would go to the forest to fetch Rama back and would serve out his term of exile himself. Although initially resentful and suspicious, people of Ayodhya hail Bharata's selfless nature and courageous act. Despite his fervent pleas to return, Rama asserts that he must stay in the forest to keep his father's word. He orders Bharata to perform his duty as king of Ayodhya, especially important after Dasharatha's death and orders Shatrughna to support and serve him. Returning saddened to the city, Bharata refuses to wear the crown or sit on the throne. Instead, he places the slippers of Rama that he had taken back with him on the throne and rules Ayodhya assiduously keeping Rama's beliefs and values in mind. When Sita is kidnapped, Rama blazes with his divine power and in his immense rage, expresses the desire to destroy all creation. Lakshmana prays and pleads for Rama to calm himself and despite the shock of the moment and the promise of travails to come, begin an arduous, but systematic search for Sita. Krishnamurti', u'\n', u'Vivekananda', u'\n', u'Yogananda', u'\n', u'Ramachandra Dattatrya Ranade', u'\n', u'Mata Amritanandamayi', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Other topics', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Calendar', u'\n', u'Criticism', u'\n', u'Denominations', u'\n', u'Iconography', u'\n', u'Mythology', u'\n', u'Nationalism', u'\xa0', u'(', u'Hindutva', u')', u'\n', u'Persecution', u'\n', u'Pilgrimage sites', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Hinduism and Jainism', u'\xa0/ ', u'and Judaism', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Hinduism by country', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Glossary of Hinduism terms', u'\n', u' ', u'Hinduism portal', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'v', u'\n', u't', u'\n', u'e', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Rama', u' (', u'/', u'\u02c8', u'r', u'\u0251\u02d0', u'm', u'\u0259', u'/', u';', u'[1]', u' ', u'Sanskrit', u': \u0930\u093e\u092e ', u'R\u0101ma', u') or ', u'Sr\u012b R\u0101machandra', u' (', u'Sanskrit', u'\xa0: \u0936\u094d\u0930\u0940 \u0930\u093e\u092e\u091a\u0928\u094d\u0926\u094d\u0930) is the ', u'seventh', u' ', u'avatar', u' of the Hindu God ', u'Vishnu', u'. He is the central figure of the ', u'Hindu epic', u' ', u'Ramayana', u', which is the principal narration of the events connected to his incarnation on Earth, his ideals and his greatness. Rama is one of the many deities in ', u'Hinduism', u' and especially of the various ', u'Vaishnava', u' sects. Religious texts and scriptures based on his life have been a formative component in numerous cultures of ', u'South', u' and ', u'Southeast Asia', u'.', u'[2]', u' Along with ', u'Krishna', u', Rama is considered to be one of the most important avatars of Vishnu. In Rama-centric sects, he is considered the Supreme Being, rather than an avatar.', u'\n', u'Born as the eldest son of ', u'Kaushalya', u' and ', u'Dasharatha', u', ruler of ', u'Kosala', u" Kingdom (now in Uttar Pradesh), Rama is referred as ''", u'Maryada Purushottama', u'"', u'[3]', u' within Hinduism, which literally means ', u'the Perfect Man', u' or ', u'Lord of Self-Control', u' or ', u'Lord of Virtue', u'. His wife ', u'Sita', u' is considered by Hindus to be an avatar of ', u'Lakshmi', u' and the embodiment of a great woman.', u'[3]', u'[4]', u'\n', u'Rama and his brothers ', u'Lakshman', u', ', u'Bharat', u', ', u'Shatrughna', u' were the "chaturvyuha" expansions of Vishnu (', u'Vasudev', u', ', u'Sankarshan', u', ', u'Pradyumna', u', ', u'Aniruddha', u"). Rama's life and journey is one of adherence to ", u'dharma', u" despite harsh tests and obstacles and many pains of life and time. For the sake of his father's honour, Rama abandons his claim to Ayodhya's throne to serve an exile of fourteen years in the forest.", u'[5]', u' His wife Sita and brother ', u'Lakshmana', u' decide to join him, and all three spend the fourteen years in exile together. While in exile, Sita is kidnapped by ', u'Ravana', u', the king of ', u'Lanka', u". After a long and arduous search, Rama fights a colossal war against Ravana's armies. In a war of powerful and magical beings, greatly destructive weaponry and battles, Rama slays ", u'Ravana', u' in battle and liberates his wife.', u'[6]', u' Having completed his exile, Rama returns to be crowned king in Ayodhya and eventually becomes emperor,', u'[5]', u' rules with happiness, peace, duty, prosperity and justice\u2014a period known as ', u'Rama Rajya', u'.', u'\n', u'The legend of Rama is deeply influential and popular in the societies of the ', u'Indian subcontinent', u' and across ', u'South East Asia', u'. Rama is revered for his unending compassion,', u'[7]', u' courage and devotion to religious values and duty. The deity ', u'Hanuman', u' declared Rama to be a supreme being, and said that, by chanting the name of Lord Rama, all earthly problems may be resolved. By chanting the name of lord Rama 10 million times, ', u'Moksha', u' can be achieved.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Contents', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'1', u' ', u'Etymology', u'\n', u'2', u' ', u'Literary sources', u'\n', u'3', u' ', u'Balkand', u'\n', u'4', u' ', u'Rama and Sita', u'\n', u'5', u' ', u"Sita's Exile", u'\n', u'\n', u'5.1', u' ', u'Children', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'6', u' ', u'Later life', u'\n', u'7', u' ', u'Abilities', u'\n', u'8', u' ', u'Maryada Purushottama', u'\n', u'9', u' ', u'Companions', u'\n', u'\n', u'9.1', u' ', u'Bharata and Lakshmana', u'\n', u'9.2', u' ', u'Jatayu, Hanuman & Vibhishana', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'10', u' ', u'Rama In War', u'\n', u'\n', u'10.1', u' ', u'Varuna', u'\n', u'10.2', u' ', u'Facing Ravana', u'\n', u'10.3', u' ', u'Rama Rajya', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'11', u' ', u'International Influence', u'\n', u'12', u' ', u'Rama Worship', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.1', u' ', u'Festivals', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.1.1', u' ', u'Rama Navami', u'\n', u'12.1.2', u' ', u'Vijayadashmi', u'\n', u'12.1.3', u' ', u'Diwali', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.2', u' ', u'Temples', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'13', u' ', u'In Jainism', u'\n', u'14', u' ', u'See also', u'\n', u'15', u' ', u'Notes', u'\n', u'16', u' ', u'References', u'\n', u'17', u' ', u'Further reading', u'\n', u'18', u' ', u'External links', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Etymology', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This article ', u'needs additional citations for ', u'verification', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'The name Rama appears repeatedly in Hindu scriptures. Besides the name of the protagonist of the ', u'Ramayana', u' (subject of the current article), the name is also given to other heroes including ', u'Parashu-Rama', u' (Bhargava Rama) and ', u'Bala-Rama', u'.', u'\n', u'In the ', u'Vishnu sahasranama', u', Rama is the 394th name of Vishnu. In the interpretation of ', u'Adi Shankara', u"'s commentary, translated by ", u'Swami Tapasyananda', u' of the ', u'Ramakrishna Mission', u', Rama has two meanings: the supreme ', u'Brahman', u' who is the eternally blissful spiritual Self in whom ', u'yogis', u' delight, and the One (i.e., Vishnu, the supreme Brahman) who out of His own will assumed the enchanting form of Rama, the son of ', u'Dasaratha', u'.', u'[8]', u'\n', u'Other names of Rama include Ramavijaya (', u'Javanese', u'), Phreah Ream (', u'Khmer', u'), Phra Ram (', u'Lao', u' and ', u'Thai', u'), Megat Seri Rama (', u'Malay', u'), Raja Bantugan (', u'Maranao', u'), Ramudu (', u'Telugu', u') and Ramar (', u'Tamil', u').', u'\n', u"The greatness of chanting of Rama's name is mentioned in the ", u'Ramacharitamanasa', u'.', u'[9]', u'[10]', u'[11]', u'[12]', u'[13]', u'[14]', u'[15]', u'\n', u'In ', u'Sanskrit', u', the word ', u'Rama', u" (\u0930\u093e\u092e) means 'charming'. The name is commonly given to male in ", u'India', u' and ', u'Nepal', u'.', u'\n', u'Some of the popular names of Rama are-', u'\n', u'\n', u'Rama - charming', u'\n', u'Ramachandra - Rama with a moon', u'\n', u'Raghava - of the lineage of ', u'Raghu', u'\n', u'Raghunandan-scion of ', u'Raghu', u'\n', u'Siyaavara - husband of Sita', u'\n', u'Ayodhyapati - king of Ayodhya', u'\n', u'Dashrathaputra - son of Dasharatha', u'\n', u'Maryada-Purushottama - best ideal man', u'\n', u'\n', u'Literary sources', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Valmiki', u' composing the Ramayana.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'The primary source of the life and journey of Rama is the epic Ramayana as composed by the ', u'Rishi', u' ', u'Valmiki', u'. The ', u'Vishnu Purana', u" also recounts Rama as Vishnu's seventh ", u'avatar', u', and in the ', u'Bhagavata Purana', u", ninth skandha, adhyayas 10 & 11, the story of the Ramayana is again recounted in brief up to and including the slaying of Ravana and Prince Rama's return to Ayodhya. Additionally, the tales of Rama are reverently spoken of in the ", u'Mahabharata', u'. The earliest documentation of Rama is in the Buddhist text of Dasharatha Jataka.', u'[16]', u'\n', u"The epic had many versions across India's regions. However, other scriptures in Sanskrit also reflect the life of Ramayana. The followers of ", u'Madhvacharya', u' believe that an older version of the Ramayana, the mula-Ramayana, previously existed. They consider it to have been more authoritative than the version by ', u'Valmiki', u'. Another important shortened version of the epic in Sanskrit is the ', u'Adhyatma Ramayana', u'. The seventh century CE Sanskrit "Bhatti\'s Poem" ', u'Bha\u1e6d\u1e6dik\u0101vya', u' of Bhatti who lived in ', u'Gujarat', u', is a retelling of the epic that simultaneously illustrates the grammatical examples for ', u'P\u0101\u1e47ini', u"'s ", u'A\u1e63\u1e6d\u0101dhy\u0101y\u012b', u' as well as the major figures of speech and the ', u'Prakrit', u' language.', u'[17]', u' Versions of the Ramayana exist in most major Indian languages; examples that elaborate on the life, deeds and divine philosophies of Rama include the epic poem ', u'Ramavataram', u' by the 12th-century poet ', u'Kambar', u' in ', u'Tamil', u', and ', u'Ramcharitmanas', u', a ', u'Hindi', u' version of the Ramayana by the 16th-century saint, ', u'Tulsidas', u'. Contemporary versions of the Ramayana include ', u'Sri Ramayana Darshanam', u' by ', u'Kuvempu', u' in ', u'Kannada', u' and ', u'Ramayana Kalpavruksham', u' by ', u'Viswanatha Satyanarayana', u' in ', u'Telugu', u', both of which have been awarded the ', u'Jnanpith Award', u'. The epic has transformed across the diverse regions of India, which boast their own unique languages and cultural traditions.', u'[18]', u' In Agastyasamhita, Lord Shiva is depicted as worshipping Lord Rama, who bestows upon him the ability to grant "moksha".', u'[19]', u'\n', u'The essential tale of Rama has also spread across ', u'Southeast Asia', u', and evolved into unique renditions of the epic \u2013 incorporating local history, folktales, religious values as well as unique features from the languages and literary discourse. The ', u'Kakawin Ramayana', u' of ', u'Java', u', ', u'Indonesia', u', the ', u'Ramakavaca', u' of ', u'Bali', u', ', u'Hikayat Seri Rama', u' of ', u'Malaysia', u', ', u'Maradia Lawana', u' of the ', u'Philippines', u', ', u'Ramakien', u' of ', u'Thailand', u' (that calls him ', u'Phra Ram', u') are great works with many unique characteristics and differences in accounts and portrayals of the legend of Rama. The legends of Rama are witnessed in elaborate illustration at the ', u'Wat Phra Kaew', u' temple in ', u'Bangkok', u'. The national epic of ', u'Myanmar', u', ', u'Yama Zatdaw', u' is essentially the Burmese ', u'Ramayana', u', where Rama is named ', u'Yama', u'. In the ', u'Reamker', u' of ', u'Cambodia', u', Rama is known as ', u'Preah Ream', u'. In the ', u'Phra Lak Phra Lam', u' of ', u'Laos', u', ', u'Gautama Buddha', u' is regarded as an incarnation of Rama.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u'To the ', u'Valmiki Ramayana', u',', u'[20]', u' Rama was born in Ayodhya, India, on 9th day (now celebrated across India as Ram Navami) of ', u'Chaitra', u' lunar month (March\u2013April), when Moon and Jupiter were rising in the east in Cancer sign and four other planets (Sun, Mars, Saturn, Venus) were exalted in their exaltation signs. Jupiter in the sign Cancer is exalted.', u'\n', u'According to ', u'Valmiki Ramayana', u' and other ancient sources, Rama was born about 880 thousand years ago, near the end of ', u'Treta Yuga', u', and eleven thousand years after his coronation, ', u'Dwapara Yuga', u' started that lasted 864,000 years, followed by ', u'Kali Yuga', u' in which 3101 years had elapsed at the beginning of Christian Era.', u'[21]', u'[22]', u'[23]', u'\n', u'Composition of ', u'Ramayana', u' in its current form is usually dated to 7th - 4th Century BCE.', u'[24]', u'[25]', u'[26]', u'\n', u'Balkand', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'See also: ', u'Reasons for Ram avatar', u' and ', u'Genealogy of Rama', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nRama(left third from top) depicted in the ', u'Dashavatara', u'(ten avatars) of Vishnu. Vashishta to the left', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u"At Mithila,Rama breaks Shiva's bow and Janaka arranges the marriage of his daughter Sita to Rama.", u'[27]', u' The ', u'Wedding of Rama and Sita', u' concerns two entities coming together to form a whole. An Indian marriage forges an alliance not only between two people, but also two families. The marriage of Sita and Rama creates an alliance between two people, two families, and two kingdoms: ', u'Mithila', u', home of Sita and ', u'Kosala', u", home of Rama. Furthermore, Rama's marriage to Sita on Earth parallels the celestial union of ", u'Vishnu', u' and ', u'Lakshmi', u'; each deity took birth on Earth, and so when Rama marries Sita, he is actually reuniting with his divine consort Lakshmi, Goddess of Good Fortune, who brings prosperity to Kosala. At an allegorical level, the union of Rama and Sita represents the relationship between God and the devotee, with Rama as the beloved divine king and Sita as his devotee. Finally, at a societal level, the dance drama brings together north and south Indian dance traditions.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u"Sita's Exile", u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nRama fighting his sons Lava and Kusha', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'In the ', u'Uttara Kanda', u", Rama banishes his wife Sita, even as she is pregnant, asking Lakshmana to deliver her safely to the forest. He does so after receiving word that some of his subjects in Ayodhya believed that Sita was unfit due to her long captivity in Ravana's city. As a king is expected to uphold moral principles, Rama reluctantly banished Sita in order to uphold his duty. Sita took refuge under the noble sage ", u'Valmiki', u'.', u'\n', u'A legend by Rishi ', u'Agastya', u' in the epic states that ', u'Vishnu', u' in a previous age had been cursed by ', u'Rishi Bhrigu', u", whose wife had been killed by Vishnu for sheltering his enemies escaping from battle. The Rishi condemns Vishnu to be denied for a long age the companionship of his soul mate, just as Vishnu, had deprived the Rishi of his loving wife. Thus Rama, Vishnu's incarnation, must live the rest of his life without Sita.", u'\n', u'Many Hindus, such as the followers of ', u'Sri Vaishnavism', u', consider this entire section of the Ramayana to be interpolated and thus they do not accept the authenticity of this story claiming that Sita was banished.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Sita', u'(far right), Rama(center), ', u'Lakshmana', u'(far left) and ', u'Hanuman', u'(below seated) at ', u'Bhaktivedanta Manor', u', a temple in Watford(England)', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'An alternate narration of ', u'Ramayana', u' does not state it so. It says that ', u'Sita', u" later lived in her father's kingdom of ", u'Mithila', u' with her sons Lava and Kusha as per the North Indian(especially in ', u'Uttar Pradesh', u' and ', u'Bihar', u') custom that children be brought up in their ', u'nanihal', u" or maternal grandmother's place. ", u'Sita', u' and her sons later live in ', u'Valmiki', u"'s ashram for the boys' education and military training. As per Tulsidas' Ramcharitmanas, both the princes grew extremely intelligent and strong under Rishi Valmiki's tutelage.", u'\n', u'Children', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Main articles: ', u'Kusha (Ramayana)', u' and ', u'Lava (Ramayana)', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nLava and Kusha, the sons of Rama', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'According to legend, ', u'Kusha', u' and ', u'Lava', u' are twin sons of Lord Rama and Sita. Born in the forest after banishment of Sita from ', u'Ayodhya', u', the twins were educated and trained in military skills as their mother took refuge in Sage ', u'Valmiki', u"'s ", u'ashram', u', located in a forest on the banks of ', u'Tamsa river', u'.', u'\n', u'As Rama performed the ', u'Ashvamedha', u' ', u'Yajna', u", a horse strayed into their forest, Rama sent Hanuman to retrieve the horses. Rama's sons Lava and Kusha captured the horses. Hanuman, seeing Lava and Kusha recognised that they were the son's of Rama. He let them capture him and tie him up. There Hanuman started meditating on the name Rama. Worried Rama sent his brothers to look for the horses. As they saw Hanuman tied up and two boys guarding him, they thought that the two boy had stolen the horses. So Rama's brothers started attacking Lava and Kusha. Although Rama's brothers should have won, but Lava and Kusha defeated them all, knocking them unconscious. Lava and Kusha were protected by Hanuman. Then Rama himself went looking for the horses fearing that Hanuman and his brothers had been attacked. On his way there, Rama intuitively knew that Lava and Kusha were his sons and purposely slept on his chariot to delay tension and confrontation with his sons as he knew it would be inappropriate for a father to fight his sons. Upon reaching the battlefield, sage Valmiki interrupted the potential battle between father and sons by explaining to Rama that Lava and Kusha were his sons. A familial reunion took place.", u'\n', u"When Devi Sita found out that Lava and Kusha had defeated Ayodhya's forces, she proudly revealed their/her identity. Rama desired Sita and his sons to live with him in his kingdom, but as this took place, the general population of the kingdom resented Sita from returning. In response, Sita forsaked her life and sought final refuge in the arms of her mother Bhumidevi, the Goddess Mother Earth and ultimately returned to Rama in the form of Vishnu in Vishnu's abode - indicating that forced separation from her beloved husband is only limited in life on Earth compared to her eternal union with her beloved in life after death.", u'\n', u'Later life', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nRishi ', u'Agastya', u'(Father of ', u'Tamil literature', u') - Rama acquired a rare gem from him that entombed the powers of the gods Indra, Varuna, Yama and Kubera', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u"Rama's reign is known as the ", u'Rama Rajya', u' that lasted for 11,000 years. During this period, people were healthy, holy, satisfied and lived with complete peace and harmony. There was no evil, no wars, no natural calamity and no diseases. Rama ruled the whole Earth without using military force as all kings submitted themselves to him.', u'\n', u'His brothers Bharata and Shatrughna settled in their later lives. Bharata, with the help of his uncle Yudhajita, conquered the eastern land of the Gandharvas and ruled it. Shatrughna slew the Asura Lavana and founded the city of Mathura. Rama acquired a rare gem from Rishi ', u'Agastya', u' that entombed the powers of the gods ', u'Indra', u', ', u'Varuna', u', ', u'Yama', u' and ', u'Kubera', u', which helped the king rule efficiently. After his reign, Rama, his brothers and his allies peacefully left the Earth on the river Saryu abandoning their mortal bodies. Valmiki Ramayana mentions an abode named ', u'Santanaka', u' invested with all spiritual qualities and located beyond Brahmaloka, which was attained by all followers of Rama, after Rama along with his brothers, entered into Vaishnava potency. Denouncing his mother, Bharata proclaims to the city that he would go to the forest to fetch Rama back and would serve out his term of exile himself. Although initially resentful and suspicious, people of Ayodhya hail Bharata's selfless nature and courageous act. Despite his fervent pleas to return, Rama asserts that he must stay in the forest to keep his father's word. He orders Bharata to perform his duty as king of Ayodhya, especially important after Dasharatha's death and orders Shatrughna to support and serve him. Returning saddened to the city, Bharata refuses to wear the crown or sit on the throne. Instead, he places the slippers of Rama that he had taken back with him on the throne and rules Ayodhya assiduously keeping Rama's beliefs and values in mind. Along with Rama, people also pray to Sita, Lakshmana and Hanuman.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Vijayadashami', u' celebrations', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Vijayadashmi', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'Main article: ', u'Vijayadashami', u'\n', u'The occasion of victory over Ravana and the rakshasas is celebrated as the 10-day ', u'Vijayadashami', u', also known as ', u'Dussehra', u'. The ', u'Rama Leela', u' is publicly performed in many villages, towns and cities in Northern India and also in places where there is a large population of North Indians. Hindus also celebrate Vijayadashmi as the day of victory of Goddess ', u'Durga', u' over the Rakshas Mahishasura.', u'\n', u'Diwali', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'Main article: ', u'Diwali', u'\n', u"In some parts of India, Rama's return to Ayodhya and his coronation is the main reason for celebrating ", u'Diwali', u', also known as the ', u'Festival of Lights', u'. In ', u'Malaysia', u', Diwali is known as ', u'Hari Deepavali', u' and is celebrated during the seventh month of the Hindu solar calendar. It is a federal public holiday. In many respects it resembles the traditions followed in the Indian subcontinent. In ', u'Nepal', u', Diwali is known as ', u'Tihar', u' and celebrated during the October/November period.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Deities', u' inside the Kalaram Temple, ', u'Nashik', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'In ', u'Guyana', u", Diwali is marked as a special occasion and celebrated with a lot of fanfare. It is observed as a national holiday in this part of the World and some ministers of the Government also take part in the celebrations publicly. Just like Vijayadashmi, Diwali is celebrated by different communities across India to commemorate different events in addition to Rama's return to Ayodhya. For example, many communities celebrate one day of Diwali to celebrate the Victory of Krishna over the demon ", u'Narakasur', u'.', u'\n', u'Temples', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'See also: ', u'List of Hindu festivals', u'\n', u'Temples dedicated to Rama are found all over India and in places where Indian migrant communities have resided. In most temples, the standing idol of Rama is accompanied by that of his wife Sita and brother Laxman. In some instances, the monkey God, ', u'Hanuman', u' sits at the feet of Rama or is situated facing the Rama family at a distance or at the entrance of the temple. There are numerous Rama temples in ', u'Tamil nadu', u' that date from the end of the first millinium of the common era.', u'[48]', u' Important Rama temples include:', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nRam, Sita, Lakshman, Hanuman, at Vallipuram Temple, Sri Lanka', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Ram Janmabhoomi', u', Ayodhya', u'\n', u'Kalaram Temple', u', Nashik - built in 1788', u'\n', u'Raghunath Temple', u', Jammu - built in 1827', u'\n', u'Ram Mandir, Bhubaneswar', u', Odisha', u'\n', u'Kodandarama Temple', u', Chikmagalur', u'\n', u'Kothandarama Temple, Thillaivilagam', u'\n', u'Kothandaramaswamy Temple', u', Rameswaram', u'\n', u'Odogaon Raghunath Temple', u', Odisha - dates from Middle Ages', u'\n', u'Ramchaura Mandir', u', Bihar', u'\n', u'Sri Rama Temple, Ramapuram', u'\n', u'Bhadrachalam Temple', u', ', u'Telangana', u' - built in 1674', u'\n', u'Shree Rama Temple', u', ', u'Triprayar', u', ', u'Kerala', u'\n', u'\n', u'In Jainism', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(October 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Main articles: ', u'Rama in Jainism', u' and ', u'Salakapurusa', u'\n', u'Rama, Lakshmana and Ravana forms one of the nine set of ', u'Baladeva', u', ', u'Vasudeva', u' and ', u'Prativasudeva', u' whose stories forms a basis of Jain universal history.', u'[49]', u'[50]', u' Rama is described as a pious layman in ', u'Jain scriptures', u". Jain scriptures tells different version of Ramayana than Valmiki's version. According to this version, Lakshmana(Vasudeva) is the one who kills Ravana(Prativasudeva). Rama(Baladeva) is described as a non-violent person who attains moksha. Lakshmana and Ravana, on the other hand, goes to ", u'hell', u' on account of their violence & will attain ', u'moksha', u' in their next birth. Ravan will take birth as ', u'tirthankara', u' of next era. It is said that in the end, Rama and Sita take Jain diksha in this version.', u'\n', u'See also', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'Genealogy of Rama', u'\n', u'Ram Nam', u'\n', u'Ramayana', u'\n', u'Ayodhya', u'\n', u'Sita', u'\n', u'\n', u'Notes', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'^', u' ', u'"Rama"', u'. Krishnamurti', u'\n', u'Vivekananda', u'\n', u'Yogananda', u'\n', u'Ramachandra Dattatrya Ranade', u'\n', u'Mata Amritanandamayi', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Other topics', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Calendar', u'\n', u'Criticism', u'\n', u'Denominations', u'\n', u'Iconography', u'\n', u'Mythology', u'\n', u'Nationalism', u'\xa0', u'(', u'Hindutva', u')', u'\n', u'Persecution', u'\n', u'Pilgrimage sites', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Hinduism and Jainism', u'\xa0/ ', u'and Judaism', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Hinduism by country', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Glossary of Hinduism terms', u'\n', u' ', u'Hinduism portal', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'v', u'\n', u't', u'\n', u'e', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Rama', u' (', u'/', u'\u02c8', u'r', u'\u0251\u02d0', u'm', u'\u0259', u'/', u';', u'[1]', u' ', u'Sanskrit', u': \u0930\u093e\u092e ', u'R\u0101ma', u') or ', u'Sr\u012b R\u0101machandra', u' (', u'Sanskrit', u'\xa0: \u0936\u094d\u0930\u0940 \u0930\u093e\u092e\u091a\u0928\u094d\u0926\u094d\u0930) is the ', u'seventh', u' ', u'avatar', u' of the Hindu God ', u'Vishnu', u'. He is the central figure of the ', u'Hindu epic', u' ', u'Ramayana', u', which is the principal narration of the events connected to his incarnation on Earth, his ideals and his greatness. Rama is one of the many deities in ', u'Hinduism', u' and especially of the various ', u'Vaishnava', u' sects. Religious texts and scriptures based on his life have been a formative component in numerous cultures of ', u'South', u' and ', u'Southeast Asia', u'.', u'[2]', u' Along with ', u'Krishna', u', Rama is considered to be one of the most important avatars of Vishnu. In Rama-centric sects, he is considered the Supreme Being, rather than an avatar.', u'\n', u'Born as the eldest son of ', u'Kaushalya', u' and ', u'Dasharatha', u', ruler of ', u'Kosala', u" Kingdom (now in Uttar Pradesh), Rama is referred as ''", u'Maryada Purushottama', u'"', u'[3]', u' within Hinduism, which literally means ', u'the Perfect Man', u' or ', u'Lord of Self-Control', u' or ', u'Lord of Virtue', u'. His wife ', u'Sita', u' is considered by Hindus to be an avatar of ', u'Lakshmi', u' and the embodiment of a great woman.', u'[3]', u'[4]', u'\n', u'Rama and his brothers ', u'Lakshman', u', ', u'Bharat', u', ', u'Shatrughna', u' were the "chaturvyuha" expansions of Vishnu (', u'Vasudev', u', ', u'Sankarshan', u', ', u'Pradyumna', u', ', u'Aniruddha', u"). Rama's life and journey is one of adherence to ", u'dharma', u" despite harsh tests and obstacles and many pains of life and time. For the sake of his father's honour, Rama abandons his claim to Ayodhya's throne to serve an exile of fourteen years in the forest.", u'[5]', u' His wife Sita and brother ', u'Lakshmana', u' decide to join him, and all three spend the fourteen years in exile together. While in exile, Sita is kidnapped by ', u'Ravana', u', the king of ', u'Lanka', u". After a long and arduous search, Rama fights a colossal war against Ravana's armies. In a war of powerful and magical beings, greatly destructive weaponry and battles, Rama slays ", u'Ravana', u' in battle and liberates his wife.', u'[6]', u' Having completed his exile, Rama returns to be crowned king in Ayodhya and eventually becomes emperor,', u'[5]', u' rules with happiness, peace, duty, prosperity and justice\u2014a period known as ', u'Rama Rajya', u'.', u'\n', u'The legend of Rama is deeply influential and popular in the societies of the ', u'Indian subcontinent', u' and across ', u'South East Asia', u'. Rama is revered for his unending compassion,', u'[7]', u' courage and devotion to religious values and duty. The deity ', u'Hanuman', u' declared Rama to be a supreme being, and said that, by chanting the name of Lord Rama, all earthly problems may be resolved. By chanting the name of lord Rama 10 million times, ', u'Moksha', u' can be achieved.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Contents', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'1', u' ', u'Etymology', u'\n', u'2', u' ', u'Literary sources', u'\n', u'3', u' ', u'Balkand', u'\n', u'4', u' ', u'Rama and Sita', u'\n', u'5', u' ', u"Sita's Exile", u'\n', u'\n', u'5.1', u' ', u'Children', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'6', u' ', u'Later life', u'\n', u'7', u' ', u'Abilities', u'\n', u'8', u' ', u'Maryada Purushottama', u'\n', u'9', u' ', u'Companions', u'\n', u'\n', u'9.1', u' ', u'Bharata and Lakshmana', u'\n', u'9.2', u' ', u'Jatayu, Hanuman & Vibhishana', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'10', u' ', u'Rama In War', u'\n', u'\n', u'10.1', u' ', u'Varuna', u'\n', u'10.2', u' ', u'Facing Ravana', u'\n', u'10.3', u' ', u'Rama Rajya', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'11', u' ', u'International Influence', u'\n', u'12', u' ', u'Rama Worship', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.1', u' ', u'Festivals', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.1.1', u' ', u'Rama Navami', u'\n', u'12.1.2', u' ', u'Vijayadashmi', u'\n', u'12.1.3', u' ', u'Diwali', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'12.2', u' ', u'Temples', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'13', u' ', u'In Jainism', u'\n', u'14', u' ', u'See also', u'\n', u'15', u' ', u'Notes', u'\n', u'16', u' ', u'References', u'\n', u'17', u' ', u'Further reading', u'\n', u'18', u' ', u'External links', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Etymology', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This article ', u'needs additional citations for ', u'verification', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'The name Rama appears repeatedly in Hindu scriptures. Besides the name of the protagonist of the ', u'Ramayana', u' (subject of the current article), the name is also given to other heroes including ', u'Parashu-Rama', u' (Bhargava Rama) and ', u'Bala-Rama', u'.', u'\n', u'In the ', u'Vishnu sahasranama', u', Rama is the 394th name of Vishnu. In the interpretation of ', u'Adi Shankara', u"'s commentary, translated by ", u'Swami Tapasyananda', u' of the ', u'Ramakrishna Mission', u', Rama has two meanings: the supreme ', u'Brahman', u' who is the eternally blissful spiritual Self in whom ', u'yogis', u' delight, and the One (i.e., Vishnu, the supreme Brahman) who out of His own will assumed the enchanting form of Rama, the son of ', u'Dasaratha', u'.', u'[8]', u'\n', u'Other names of Rama include Ramavijaya (', u'Javanese', u'), Phreah Ream (', u'Khmer', u'), Phra Ram (', u'Lao', u' and ', u'Thai', u'), Megat Seri Rama (', u'Malay', u'), Raja Bantugan (', u'Maranao', u'), Ramudu (', u'Telugu', u') and Ramar (', u'Tamil', u').', u'\n', u"The greatness of chanting of Rama's name is mentioned in the ", u'Ramacharitamanasa', u'.', u'[9]', u'[10]', u'[11]', u'[12]', u'[13]', u'[14]', u'[15]', u'\n', u'In ', u'Sanskrit', u', the word ', u'Rama', u" (\u0930\u093e\u092e) means 'charming'. The name is commonly given to male in ", u'India', u' and ', u'Nepal', u'.', u'\n', u'Some of the popular names of Rama are-', u'\n', u'\n', u'Rama - charming', u'\n', u'Ramachandra - Rama with a moon', u'\n', u'Raghava - of the lineage of ', u'Raghu', u'\n', u'Raghunandan-scion of ', u'Raghu', u'\n', u'Siyaavara - husband of Sita', u'\n', u'Ayodhyapati - king of Ayodhya', u'\n', u'Dashrathaputra - son of Dasharatha', u'\n', u'Maryada-Purushottama - best ideal man', u'\n', u'\n', u'Literary sources', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Valmiki', u' composing the Ramayana.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'The primary source of the life and journey of Rama is the epic Ramayana as composed by the ', u'Rishi', u' ', u'Valmiki', u'. The ', u'Vishnu Purana', u" also recounts Rama as Vishnu's seventh ", u'avatar', u', and in the ', u'Bhagavata Purana', u", ninth skandha, adhyayas 10 & 11, the story of the Ramayana is again recounted in brief up to and including the slaying of Ravana and Prince Rama's return to Ayodhya. Additionally, the tales of Rama are reverently spoken of in the ", u'Mahabharata', u'. The earliest documentation of Rama is in the Buddhist text of Dasharatha Jataka.', u'[16]', u'\n', u"The epic had many versions across India's regions. However, other scriptures in Sanskrit also reflect the life of Ramayana. The followers of ", u'Madhvacharya', u' believe that an older version of the Ramayana, the mula-Ramayana, previously existed. They consider it to have been more authoritative than the version by ', u'Valmiki', u'. Another important shortened version of the epic in Sanskrit is the ', u'Adhyatma Ramayana', u'. The seventh century CE Sanskrit "Bhatti\'s Poem" ', u'Bha\u1e6d\u1e6dik\u0101vya', u' of Bhatti who lived in ', u'Gujarat', u', is a retelling of the epic that simultaneously illustrates the grammatical examples for ', u'P\u0101\u1e47ini', u"'s ", u'A\u1e63\u1e6d\u0101dhy\u0101y\u012b', u' as well as the major figures of speech and the ', u'Prakrit', u' language.', u'[17]', u' Versions of the Ramayana exist in most major Indian languages; examples that elaborate on the life, deeds and divine philosophies of Rama include the epic poem ', u'Ramavataram', u' by the 12th-century poet ', u'Kambar', u' in ', u'Tamil', u', and ', u'Ramcharitmanas', u', a ', u'Hindi', u' version of the Ramayana by the 16th-century saint, ', u'Tulsidas', u'. Contemporary versions of the Ramayana include ', u'Sri Ramayana Darshanam', u' by ', u'Kuvempu', u' in ', u'Kannada', u' and ', u'Ramayana Kalpavruksham', u' by ', u'Viswanatha Satyanarayana', u' in ', u'Telugu', u', both of which have been awarded the ', u'Jnanpith Award', u'. The epic has transformed across the diverse regions of India, which boast their own unique languages and cultural traditions.', u'[18]', u' In Agastyasamhita, Lord Shiva is depicted as worshipping Lord Rama, who bestows upon him the ability to grant "moksha".', u'[19]', u'\n', u'The essential tale of Rama has also spread across ', u'Southeast Asia', u', and evolved into unique renditions of the epic \u2013 incorporating local history, folktales, religious values as well as unique features from the languages and literary discourse. The ', u'Kakawin Ramayana', u' of ', u'Java', u', ', u'Indonesia', u', the ', u'Ramakavaca', u' of ', u'Bali', u', ', u'Hikayat Seri Rama', u' of ', u'Malaysia', u', ', u'Maradia Lawana', u' of the ', u'Philippines', u', ', u'Ramakien', u' of ', u'Thailand', u' (that calls him ', u'Phra Ram', u') are great works with many unique characteristics and differences in accounts and portrayals of the legend of Rama. The legends of Rama are witnessed in elaborate illustration at the ', u'Wat Phra Kaew', u' temple in ', u'Bangkok', u'. The national epic of ', u'Myanmar', u', ', u'Yama Zatdaw', u' is essentially the Burmese ', u'Ramayana', u', where Rama is named ', u'Yama', u'. In the ', u'Reamker', u' of ', u'Cambodia', u', Rama is known as ', u'Preah Ream', u'. In the ', u'Phra Lak Phra Lam', u' of ', u'Laos', u', ', u'Gautama Buddha', u' is regarded as an incarnation of Rama.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u'To the ', u'Valmiki Ramayana', u',', u'[20]', u' Rama was born in Ayodhya, India, on 9th day (now celebrated across India as Ram Navami) of ', u'Chaitra', u' lunar month (March\u2013April), when Moon and Jupiter were rising in the east in Cancer sign and four other planets (Sun, Mars, Saturn, Venus) were exalted in their exaltation signs. Jupiter in the sign Cancer is exalted.', u'\n', u'According to ', u'Valmiki Ramayana', u' and other ancient sources, Rama was born about 880 thousand years ago, near the end of ', u'Treta Yuga', u', and eleven thousand years after his coronation, ', u'Dwapara Yuga', u' started that lasted 864,000 years, followed by ', u'Kali Yuga', u' in which 3101 years had elapsed at the beginning of Christian Era.', u'[21]', u'[22]', u'[23]', u'\n', u'Composition of ', u'Ramayana', u' in its current form is usually dated to 7th - 4th Century BCE.', u'[24]', u'[25]', u'[26]', u'\n', u'Balkand', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'See also: ', u'Reasons for Ram avatar', u' and ', u'Genealogy of Rama', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nRama(left third from top) depicted in the ', u'Dashavatara', u'(ten avatars) of Vishnu. Vashishta to the left', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u"At Mithila,Rama breaks Shiva's bow and Janaka arranges the marriage of his daughter Sita to Rama.", u'[27]', u' The ', u'Wedding of Rama and Sita', u' concerns two entities coming together to form a whole. An Indian marriage forges an alliance not only between two people, but also two families. The marriage of Sita and Rama creates an alliance between two people, two families, and two kingdoms: ', u'Mithila', u', home of Sita and ', u'Kosala', u", home of Rama. Furthermore, Rama's marriage to Sita on Earth parallels the celestial union of ", u'Vishnu', u' and ', u'Lakshmi', u'; each deity took birth on Earth, and so when Rama marries Sita, he is actually reuniting with his divine consort Lakshmi, Goddess of Good Fortune, who brings prosperity to Kosala. At an allegorical level, the union of Rama and Sita represents the relationship between God and the devotee, with Rama as the beloved divine king and Sita as his devotee. Finally, at a societal level, the dance drama brings together north and south Indian dance traditions.', u'[', u'citation needed', u']', u'\n', u"Sita's Exile", u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'This section ', u'does not ', u'cite', u' any ', u'sources', u'. ', u'Please help improve this section by ', u'adding citations to reliable sources', u'. Unsourced material may be challenged and ', u'removed', u'.', u' ', u'(May 2016)', u' ', u'(', u'Learn how and when to remove this template message', u')', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nRama fighting his sons Lava and Kusha', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'In the ', u'Uttara Kanda', u", Rama banishes his wife Sita, even as she is pregnant, asking Lakshmana to deliver her safely to the forest. He does so after receiving word that some of his subjects in Ayodhya believed that Sita was unfit due to her long captivity in Ravana's city. As a king is expected to uphold moral principles, Rama reluctantly banished Sita in order to uphold his duty. Sita took refuge under the noble sage ", u'Valmiki', u'.', u'\n', u'A legend by Rishi ', u'Agastya', u' in the epic states that ', u'Vishnu', u' in a previous age had been cursed by ', u'Rishi Bhrigu', u", whose wife had been killed by Vishnu for sheltering his enemies escaping from battle. The Rishi condemns Vishnu to be denied for a long age the companionship of his soul mate, just as Vishnu, had deprived the Rishi of his loving wife. Thus Rama, Vishnu's incarnation, must live the rest of his life without Sita.", u'\n', u'Many Hindus, such as the followers of ', u'Sri Vaishnavism', u', consider this entire section of the Ramayana to be interpolated and thus they do not accept the authenticity of this story claiming that Sita was banished.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Sita', u'(far right), Rama(center), ', u'Lakshmana', u'(far left) and ', u'Hanuman', u'(below seated) at ', u'Bhaktivedanta Manor', u', a temple in Watford(England)', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'An alternate narration of ', u'Ramayana', u' does not state it so. There Hanuman started meditating on the name Rama. Worried Rama sent his brothers to look for the horses. As they saw Hanuman tied up and two boys guarding him, they thought that the two boy had stolen the horses. So Rama's brothers started attacking Lava and Kusha. Mathali, Indra's charioteer who had been sent by Indra after being counselled by the witnessing Rishis, Danavas and Devas. Rama fired an arrow into Ravana's chest/stomach and evaporated the store of amrit, finally killing him. Hundreds of towns and villages are named after Rama.', u'[45]', u'[46]', u'\n', u'Rama is a great hero to the adherents of ', u'Agama Hindu Dharma', u' and to the ', u'Muslims', u' who practice ', u'Abangan', u', a syncretic form of ', u'Islam', u' and ', u'Hinduism', u', in ', u'Indonesia', u'. He is revered by the people throughout ', u'Indochina', u' who otherwise adhere to different forms of ', u'Buddhism', u', ', u'Islam', u' and ', u'Hinduism', u'. The ', u'Rama Leela', u' is performed across ', u'South East Asia', u' in numerous local languages and the story has been the subject of art, architecture, music, folk dance and sculpture. The ancient city of ', u'Ayutthaya', u' stands in ', u'Thailand', u', as the tribute of an ancient Thai kingdom to the great legend. Many ancient and medieval era kings of ', u'India', u' and ', u'South East Asia', u' have adopted ', u'Rama', u' as their name.', u'\n', u'Rama Worship', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'Festivals', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'See also: ', u'List of Hindu festivals', u'\n', u'Rama Navami', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'Main article: ', u'Rama Navami', u'\n', u"Rama's day and time of birth,", u'[47]', u' as well as marriage to Sita are celebrated by Hindus across the World as ', u'Rama Navami', u'. It falls on the ninth day of a Hindu lunar year or ', u'Chaitra Masa Suklapaksha Navami', u'. This day is observed as the marriage day of Rama and Sita as well as the birthday of Rama. People normally perform ', u'Kalyanotsavam', u'(marriage celebration) for small statues of Rama and Sita in their houses and at the end of the day the idols are taken in a procession on the streets. This day also marks the end of nine-day Festival celebrated in Karnataka and Andhra Pradesh called Vasanthothsavam(Festival of Spring), that starts with ', u'Ugadi', u'. Some highlights of this day are:', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\nA Home shrine with images of Rama, ', u'Sita', u', ', u'Lakshmana', u' and ', u'Hanuman', u', on Sri ', u'Rama Navami', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Kalyanam', u'(Ceremonial wedding performed by temple priests) at ', u'Bhadrachalam', u' on the banks of the river ', u'Godavari', u' in ', u'Bhadradri Kothagudem', u' district of ', u'Telangana', u'.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Panakam', u', a sweet drink prepared on this day with jaggery and pepper.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Procession of idols in the evening that is accompanied with play of water and colours.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'For the occasion, Hindus are supposed to fast(or restrict themselves to a specific diet).', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Temples are decorated and readings of the Ramayana take place. In ', u'Malaysia', u', Diwali is known as ', u'Hari Deepavali', u' and is celebrated during the seventh month of the Hindu solar calendar. It is a federal public holiday. In many respects it resembles the traditions followed in the Indian subcontinent. In ', u'Nepal', u', Diwali is known as ', u'Tihar', u' and celebrated during the October/November period.', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'Deities', u' inside the Kalaram Temple, ', u'Nashik', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'In ', u'Guyana', u", Diwali is marked as a special occasion and celebrated with a lot of fanfare. It is observed as a national holiday in this part of the World and some ministers of the Government also take part in the celebrations publicly. Just like Vijayadashmi, Diwali is celebrated by different communities across India to commemorate different events in addition to Rama's return to Ayodhya. For example, many communities celebrate one day of Diwali to celebrate the Victory of Krishna over the demon ", u'Narakasur', u'.', u'\n', u'Temples', u'[', u'edit', u']', u'\n', u'See also: ', u'List of Hindu festivals', u'\n', u'Temples dedicated to Rama are found all over India and in places where Indian migrant communities have resided.
